   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the islands of the sovereign state, see <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">Saint Vincent (Antilles)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Saint Vincent (disambiguation)">Saint Vincent (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grenadine_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Grenadine (disambiguation)">Grenadine (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Island state in the Windward Islands in the Caribbean
      </div>

      <p><b>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'z' in 'zoom'">z</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/ce/En-us-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Saint Vincent and the Grenadines.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>), also frequently <a href="/wiki/Pars_pro_toto#Geography" title="Pars pro toto">known simply as</a> <b>Saint Vincent</b>, is an island country in the Caribbean. It's located in the southeast <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, which lies in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> at the southern end of the eastern border of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> where the latter meets the Atlantic Ocean. </p>
      <p>Its 369&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (142&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) territory consists of the main island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(Antilles)" title="Saint Vincent (Antilles)">Saint Vincent</a> and the northern two-thirds of the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a>, a chain of 32 smaller islands. Some of the Grenadines are inhabited&nbsp;— <a href="/wiki/Bequia" title="Bequia">Bequia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustique" title="Mustique">Mustique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_Island" title="Union Island">Union Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canouan" title="Canouan">Canouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petit_Saint_Vincent" title="Petit Saint Vincent">Petit Saint Vincent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_Island,_Grenadines" title="Palm Island, Grenadines">Palm Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayreau" title="Mayreau">Mayreau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Island_(Grenadines)" title="Young Island (Grenadines)">Young Island</a>&nbsp;— while others are not: <a href="/wiki/Tobago_Cays" title="Tobago Cays">Tobago Cays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baliceaux" title="Baliceaux">Baliceaux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battowia" title="Battowia">Battowia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quatre" title="Quatre">Quatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petite_Mustique" title="Petite Mustique">Petite Mustique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savan_(island)" title="Savan (island)">Savan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petit_Nevis" title="Petit Nevis">Petit Nevis</a>. Most of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines lies within the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Alley" title="Hurricane Alley">Hurricane Alley</a>. </p>
      <p>To the north of Saint Vincent lies <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, to the east is <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> lies to the south. Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is a densely populated country for its size (over 300 inhabitants/km<sup>2</sup>) with approximately 110,211 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Kingstown" title="Kingstown">Kingstown</a> is the capital and main port. Saint Vincent has a <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British colonial</a> history, and is now part of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">CARICOM</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bolivarian_Alliance_for_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas">Bolivarian Alliance for the Americas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a> (CELAC). </p>

         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Political_culture"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Political culture</span></a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, the first European to reach the island, named it after <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_of_Saragossa" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent of Saragossa">St. Vincent of Saragossa</a>, whose feast day it was on the day Columbus first saw it (22 January 1498). The name of the Grenadines refers to the Spanish city of <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>, but to differentiate it from the island of the same name, the diminutive was used. Before the arrival of the Spaniards, the Carib natives who inhabited the island of St. Vincent called it Youloumain, in honour of Youlouca, the spirit of the rainbows, who they believed inhabited the island.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="History of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">History of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_period">Pre-colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Before the arrival of Europeans and Africans in the 16th century, various <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> groups passed through or settled on <a href="/wiki/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Vincent and the Grenadines">St. Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Ciboney" title="Ciboney">Ciboney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arawaks" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawaks">Arawak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Carib</a> people.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The island now known as Saint Vincent was originally named <a href="/w/index.php?title=Youloumain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Youloumain (page does not exist)">Youloumain</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> by the native <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Caribs">Island Caribs</a> who called themselves Kalina/Carina ("l" and "r" being pronounced the same in their language).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_arrival_and_early_colonial_period">European arrival and early colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: European arrival and early colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>It is thought that <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> sighted the island in 1498, giving it the name St Vincent.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> The indigenous <a href="/wiki/Garifuna" title="Garifuna">Garifuna</a> people, who became known as the "Black Caribs", aggressively prevented European settlement on Saint Vincent.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_and_British_colonisation_and_the_First_Carib_War">French and British colonisation and the First Carib War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French and British colonisation and the First Carib War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Various attempts by the English and Dutch to claim the island proved unsuccessful, and it was the French who were first able to colonise the island, settling in the town of <a href="/wiki/Barrouallie" title="Barrouallie">Barrouallie</a> on the leeward side of St Vincent in 1719.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> The French brought with them enslaved African prisoners of war to work the plantations of sugar, coffee, indigo, tobacco, cotton and cocoa.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg/170px-SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg/255px-SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg/340px-SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="760"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SaintVincent_Carib_Treaty_Negotiation_1773.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Depiction of the 1773 treaty negotiations between the British and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Carib" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Carib">Black Caribs</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The British captured the island and drove out the French from Barrouallie during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, a claim confirmed with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> On taking control of the island in 1763, the British laid the foundations of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Charlotte,_Saint_Vincent" title="Fort Charlotte, Saint Vincent">Fort Charlotte</a> and also brought with them enslaved African prisoners of war to work on the island plantations. The Black Caribs however, opposed to the British presence, went into open conflict against the British, starting the <a href="/wiki/First_Carib_War" title="First Carib War">First Carib War</a> which lasted from 1772 to 1773.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-French_War_(1778%E2%80%931783)" title="Anglo-French War (1778–1783)">Anglo-French War (1778–1783)</a> the French <a href="/wiki/French_capture_of_Saint_Vincent" class="mw-redirect" title="French capture of Saint Vincent">recaptured St Vincent</a> in 1779. However, the British regained control under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles_(1783)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Versailles (1783)">Treaty of Versailles (1783)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_colonial_period_and_the_Second_Carib_War">British colonial period and the Second Carib War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: British colonial period and the Second Carib War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/British_Windward_Islands" title="British Windward Islands">British Windward Islands</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The uneasy peace between the British and the Black Caribs led to the <a href="/wiki/Second_Carib_War" title="Second Carib War">Second Carib War</a>, which lasted from 1795 to 1796.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> The Black Caribs were led by <a href="/wiki/Garifuna" title="Garifuna">Garifuna</a> Paramount Chief <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Chatoyer" title="Joseph Chatoyer">Joseph Chatoyer</a> and they were supported by the French, notably the radical <a href="/wiki/Victor_Hugues" title="Victor Hugues">Victor Hugues</a> from the island of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>. Their revolt and uprising was eventually put to an end in 1797 by British General Sir <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Abercromby" title="Ralph Abercromby">Ralph Abercromby</a>; a peace treaty agreement was made which resulted in almost 5,000 Black Caribs being exiled to <a href="/wiki/Roat%C3%A1n" title="Roatán">Roatán</a>, an island off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, and to <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baliceaux" title="Baliceaux">Baliceaux</a> in the Grenadines.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1806 the building of Fort Charlotte was completed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The volcano <a href="/wiki/La_Soufri%C3%A8re_(volcano)" title="La Soufrière (volcano)">La Soufrière</a> erupted in 1812, resulting in considerable destruction<sup id="cite_ref-Pyle,_David_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pyle,_David-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_(1907-1979).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_%281907-1979%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_(1907-1979).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Colonial flag (to 1979)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The British <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">abolished</a> slavery in Saint Vincent (as well as in the other <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a> colonies) in 1834, and an apprenticeship period followed which ended in 1838.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> After its end, labour shortages on the plantations resulted, and this was initially addressed by the immigration of indentured servants; in the late 1840s many Portuguese immigrants arrived from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and between 1861 and 1888 shiploads of Indian labourers arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> Conditions remained harsh for both former slaves and immigrant agricultural workers, as depressed world sugar prices kept the economy stagnant until the turn of the century. The economy then went into a period of decline with many landowners abandoning their estates and leaving the land to be cultivated by liberated slaves.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Opobo" title="Opobo">Opobo</a> king <a href="/wiki/Jaja_of_Opobo" title="Jaja of Opobo">Jaja</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> was exiled to <span class="nowrap">St. Vincent</span> after his 1887 arrest by the British for shipping cargoes of <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a> directly to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> without the intermediation of the <a href="/wiki/National_African_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="National African Company">National African Company</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png/220px-Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png/330px-Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png/440px-Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png 2x" data-file-width="496" data-file-height="494"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Baking_bread_in_the_West_Indies.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Residents of Saint Vincent making <a href="/wiki/Tapioca#Flatbreads" title="Tapioca"><i>casabe</i></a> (casava bread) in the 1910s
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1902, the volcano <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_(volcano)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufrière (volcano)">La Soufrière</a> erupted, killing 1,500–2,000 people; much farmland was damaged, and the economy deteriorated.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pyle,_David_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pyle,_David-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines passed through various stages of colonial status under the British. A representative assembly was authorised in 1776, Crown Colony government was installed in 1877, a <a href="/wiki/Legislative_council" title="Legislative council">legislative council</a> was created in 1925 with a limited franchise,<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal adult suffrage</a> was granted in 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> During the period of its control of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines, Britain made several attempts to unify the island with other Windward Islands as a single entity, with the aim of simplifying British control in that sub-region through a single unified administration.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> In the 1960s, the British again tried to unify all of its regional islands including Saint Vincent into one united single entity under British control, unified politically. The unification was to be called the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> and was driven by a desire to gain independence from British government. However, the attempt collapsed in 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Vincent was granted "associate statehood" status by Britain on 27 October 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> This gave Saint Vincent complete control over its own internal affairs but was short of full independence in law.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In April 1979 La Soufrière erupted again. Although no one was killed, thousands were evacuated and again there was extensive agricultural damage.<sup id="cite_ref-Pyle,_David_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pyle,_David-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 27 October 1979 Saint Vincent and the Grenadines became the last of the Windward Islands to gain full independence,<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> and this date is now the country's <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_independence_days" title="List of national independence days">Independence Day</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Public holidays in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">public holiday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> The country opted to remain within the <a href="/wiki/British_Commonwealth" class="mw-redirect" title="British Commonwealth">British Commonwealth</a>, retaining Queen Elizabeth as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Monarchy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Monarch</a>, represented locally by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Governor-General of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Governor-General</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-independence_era">Post-independence era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Post-independence era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sir_James_Mitchell_SVG.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sir_James_Mitchell_SVG.png/220px-Sir_James_Mitchell_SVG.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="276" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Sir_James_Mitchell_SVG.png/330px-Sir_James_Mitchell_SVG.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/05/Sir_James_Mitchell_SVG.png 2x" data-file-width="409" data-file-height="514"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sir_James_Mitchell_SVG.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>James Fitz-Allen Mitchell, the Vincentian prime minister from 1984 to 2000
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Milton_Cato" title="Milton Cato">Milton Cato</a> of the centre-left <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_Labour_Party" title="Saint Vincent Labour Party">Saint Vincent Labour Party</a> (SVLP) was the country's first Prime Minister (he had been Premier since 1974), ruling until he was defeated in the <a href="/wiki/1984_Vincentian_general_election" title="1984 Vincentian general election">1984 Vincentian general election</a> by <a href="/wiki/James_Fitz-Allen_Mitchell" title="James Fitz-Allen Mitchell">James Fitz-Allen Mitchell</a> of the centre-right <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_(Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines)" title="New Democratic Party (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)">New Democratic Party</a> (NDP).<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> During Cato's time in office there was a brief rebellion on <a href="/wiki/Union_Island" title="Union Island">Union Island</a> in December 1979 led by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lennox_%27Bumba%27_Charles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lennox 'Bumba' Charles (page does not exist)">Lennox 'Bumba' Charles</a>; apparently inspired by the recent revolution on Grenada, Charles alleged neglect of Union by the central government. However, the revolt was swiftly put down and Charles arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> There were also a series of strikes in the early 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> James Mitchell remained Prime Minister for 16 years until 2000, winning three consecutive <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Elections in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">elections</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> Mitchell was at the forefront of attempts to improve regional integration.<sup id="cite_ref-thecommonwealth.org_7-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thecommonwealth.org-7">[7]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Allen" title="Hurricane Allen">1980</a> and 1987 hurricanes damaged many banana and coconut plantations. Hurricane seasons were also very active in 1998 and 1999, with <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lenny" title="Hurricane Lenny">Hurricane Lenny</a> in 1999 causing extensive damage to the west coast of the island. </p>
      <p>In 2000 <a href="/wiki/Arnhim_Eustace" title="Arnhim Eustace">Arnhim Eustace</a> became Prime Minister after taking over the leadership of the NDP following Mitchell's retirement; he was <a href="/wiki/2001_Vincentian_general_election" title="2001 Vincentian general election">defeated</a> a year later by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Gonsalves" title="Ralph Gonsalves">Ralph Gonsalves</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Unity_Labour_Party" title="Unity Labour Party">Unity Labour Party</a> (the successor party to the SVLP).<sup id="cite_ref-caribbeanelections2001_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caribbeanelections2001-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> Gonsalves—a left-winger known in the country as "Comrade Ralph"<sup id="cite_ref-BBCLeaders_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCLeaders-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>—has argued that European nations owe Caribbean nations <a href="/wiki/Reparations_for_slavery" title="Reparations for slavery">reparations</a> for their role in the Atlantic slave trade.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Gonsalves won a second term in 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCLeaders_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCLeaders-18">[18]</a></sup> a third term in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-BBCLeaders_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCLeaders-18">[18]</a></sup> and a fourth term in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Vincentian_constitutional_referendum,_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Vincentian constitutional referendum, 2009">a referendum was held on a proposal to adopt a new constitution</a> that would make the country a <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, replacing Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as head of state with a non-executive President, a proposal supported by Prime Minister Gonsalves. A two-thirds majority was required, and it was defeated by 29,019 votes (55.64 per cent) to 22,493 (43.13 per cent).<sup id="cite_ref-antillean_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-antillean-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_11-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-11">[11]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Geography of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Geography of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg/220px-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg/330px-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg/440px-Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="612" data-file-height="792"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent Island">Saint Vincent</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines lies to the west of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> and north of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Island_arc" title="Island arc">island arc</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>. The islands of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines include the main island of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_(island)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent (island)">Saint Vincent</a> 344&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (133&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and the northern two-thirds of the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a> 45&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (17&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), which are a chain of smaller islands stretching south from Saint Vincent to Grenada. There are 32 islands and cays that make up St Vincent and the Grenadines (SVG). Nine are inhabited, including the mainland St Vincent and the Grenadines islands: Young Island, <a href="/wiki/Bequia" title="Bequia">Bequia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustique" title="Mustique">Mustique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canouan" title="Canouan">Canouan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_Island" title="Union Island">Union Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mayreau" title="Mayreau">Mayreau</a>, Petit St Vincent and Palm Island. Prominent uninhabited islands of the Grenadines include <a href="/wiki/Petit_Nevis" title="Petit Nevis">Petit Nevis</a>, used by <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whalers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petite_Mustique" title="Petite Mustique">Petit Mustique</a>, which was the centre of a prominent real-estate scam in the early 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The capital of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is <a href="/wiki/Kingstown" title="Kingstown">Kingstown</a>, Saint Vincent.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> The main island of Saint Vincent measures 26&nbsp;km (16&nbsp;mi) long, 15&nbsp;km (9.3&nbsp;mi) in width and 344&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (133&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in area. From the most northern to the most southern points, the Grenadine islands belonging to Saint Vincent span 60.4&nbsp;km (37.5&nbsp;mi), with a combined area of 45&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (17&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The island of Saint Vincent is volcanic and heavily forested, and includes little level ground.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> The windward side of the island is very rocky and steep, while the leeward side has more sandy beaches and bays.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Saint Vincent's highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_(volcano)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufrière (volcano)">La Soufrière</a> volcano at 1,234&nbsp;m (4,049&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> Other major mountains on St Vincent are (from north to south) <a href="/w/index.php?title=Richmond_Peak,_St_Vincent&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Richmond Peak, St Vincent (page does not exist)">Richmond Peak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Brisbane" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Brisbane">Mount Brisbane</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Colonarie_Mountain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Colonarie Mountain (page does not exist)">Colonarie Mountain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Bonhomme" title="Grand Bonhomme">Grand Bonhomme</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Petit_Bonhomme,_St_Vincent&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Petit Bonhomme, St Vincent (page does not exist)">Petit Bonhomme</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mount_St_Andrew&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mount St Andrew (page does not exist)">Mount St Andrew</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The country is home to three terrestrial ecoregions: Windward Islands moist forests, Leeward Islands dry forests, and Windward Islands dry forests.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-24">[24]</a></sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 6.95/10, ranking it 61<sup>st</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Politics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Politics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ralph_Gonsalves_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg/190px-Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg/285px-Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg/380px-Ralph_Gonsalves_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1762" data-file-height="1492"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ralph_Gonsalves_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ralph_Gonsalves" title="Ralph Gonsalves">Ralph Gonsalves</a>, Prime Minister of St Vincent and the Grenadines since 2001
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">constitutional monarchy</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> as <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Queen of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> She does not reside in the islands and is represented as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> in the country by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Governor-General of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Governor-General of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Susan_Dougan" title="Susan Dougan">Susan Dougan</a> (since 1 August 2019).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The office of Governor-General has mostly ceremonial functions including the opening of the islands' <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="House of Assembly of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">House of Assembly</a> and the appointment of various government officials. Control of the government rests with the elected <a href="/wiki/List_of_prime_ministers_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="List of prime ministers of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Prime Minister</a> and his or her cabinet. The current Prime Minister is <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Gonsalves" title="Ralph Gonsalves">Ralph Gonsalves</a>, elected in 2001 as head of the <a href="/wiki/Unity_Labour_Party" title="Unity Labour Party">Unity Labour Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The legislative branch of government is the unicameral <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="House of Assembly of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">House of Assembly of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, seating 15 elected members representing single-member <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">constituencies</a> and six appointed members known as Senators. The parliamentary term of office is five years, although the Prime Minister may call elections at any time.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The judicial branch of government is divided into district courts, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Caribbean_Supreme_Court" title="Eastern Caribbean Supreme Court">Eastern Caribbean Supreme Court</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Privy Council">Privy Council</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> being the court of last resort.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The two political parties with parliamentary representation are the <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_(Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines)" title="New Democratic Party (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)">New Democratic Party</a> (NDP) and the <a href="/wiki/Unity_Labour_Party" title="Unity Labour Party">Unity Labour Party</a> (ULP). The parliamentary opposition is made up of the largest minority stakeholder in the general elections, headed by the <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(parliamentary)" class="mw-redirect" title="Opposition (parliamentary)">leader of the opposition</a>. The current opposition leader is <a href="/wiki/Godwin_Friday" title="Godwin Friday">Godwin Friday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Military of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Military of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Saint Vincent has no formal armed forces, although the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Police_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Saint Vincent and the Grenadines Police Force">Royal Saint Vincent and the Grenadines Police Force</a> includes a Special Service Unit as well as a militia that has a supporting role on the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Saint Vincent signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Parishes of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Parishes of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Administratively, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is divided into six <a href="/wiki/Parish_(country_subdivision)" class="mw-redirect" title="Parish (country subdivision)">parishes</a>. Five parishes are on Saint Vincent, while the sixth is made up of the Grenadine islands. <a href="/wiki/Kingstown" title="Kingstown">Kingstown</a> is located in the Parish of Saint George and is the capital city and central administrative centre of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: LGBT rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="LGBT rights in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">LGBT rights in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Acts of gross indecency, which may be defined to include <a href="/wiki/Homosexual_activity" class="mw-redirect" title="Homosexual activity">homosexual activity</a>, are illegal in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Section 148 of the Criminal Code states: </p> 
      <blockquote>
       <p> Any person, who in public or private, commits an act of gross indecency with another person of the same sex, or procures or attempts to procure another person of the same sex to commit an act of gross indecency with him or her, is guilty of an offence and liable to imprisonment for five years.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
      </blockquote> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Foreign relations of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Foreign relations of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_and_regional_relationships">International and regional relationships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: International and regional relationships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Saint Vincent and the Grenadines maintains close ties to <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">US</a>, and cooperates with regional political and economic organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Eastern_Caribbean_States" title="Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States">Organisation of Eastern Caribbean States</a> (OECS) and <a href="/wiki/CARICOM" class="mw-redirect" title="CARICOM">CARICOM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-31">[31]</a></sup> The island nation's sixth embassy overseas was opened on 8 August 2019 in Taipei, after Prime Minister Ralph Gonsalves' official visit to the Republic of China; the other five are located in London, Washington D.C., Havana, Caracas and Brussels.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_.28CARICOM.29_Treaty"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Double_Taxation_Relief_(CARICOM)_Treaty">The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: The Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 6 July 1994 at Sherbourne Conference Centre, St Michael, Barbados, as a representative of the Government of St. Vincent and the Grenadines, then (James Mitchell, who was subsequently knighted) signed the Double Taxation Relief (CARICOM) Treaties.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-31">[31]</a></sup> There were seven other signatories to the agreement on that day. The countries which were represented were Antigua and Barbuda, Belize, Grenada, Jamaica, St Kitts and Nevis, St Lucia, and Trinidad and Tobago.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>An eighth country signed the agreement on 19 August 2016, Guyana.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>This treaty covered taxes, residence, tax jurisdictions, capital gains, business profits, interest, dividends, royalties and other areas.<sup id="cite_ref-ird.gov.tt_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ird.gov.tt-31">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="FATCA">FATCA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: FATCA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>On 30 June 2014, St. Vincent and the Grenadines signed a Model 1 agreement with the United States of America with respect to Foreign Account Tax Compliance (Act) or FATCA.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the updated site as of 16 January 2017, on 13 May 2016 the agreement went to "In Force" status.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_and_regional_bodies_to_which_St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_belong">International and regional bodies to which St. Vincent and the Grenadines belong</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: International and regional bodies to which St. Vincent and the Grenadines belong">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>St Vincent and the Grenadines is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Caribbean_States" title="Association of Caribbean States">Association of Caribbean States</a> (ACS). </p>
      <p>In September 2017, at the <a href="/wiki/Seventy-second_session_of_the_United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="Seventy-second session of the United Nations General Assembly">72nd Session of the UN General Assembly</a>, the Prime Ministers of the Solomon Islands, Tuvalu, Vanuatu and Saint Vincent and the Grenadines called for UN action on alleged human rights abuses committed on <a href="/wiki/Western_New_Guinea" title="Western New Guinea">Western New Guinea</a>'s indigenous Papuans.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Western New Guinea has been occupied by <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> since 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> More than 100,000 Papuans have died during a 50-year <a href="/wiki/Papua_conflict" title="Papua conflict">Papua conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_of_American_States">Organisation of American States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Organisation of American States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The Charter of the OAS was signed in Bogotá in 1948 and was amended by several Protocols which were named after the city and the year in which the Protocol was signed, such as "Managua" in "1993" forming part of the name of the Protocol.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>St Vincent and the Grenadines entered the OAS system on 27 October 1981 according to the OAS website.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Summits_of_the_Americas">Summits of the Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Summits of the Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>The last Summits of the Americas, the seventh, was held in Panama City, Panama in 2015 with the eighth summit being held in Lima, Peru in 2018 according to the website of the Summits of Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h5><span id="Indigenous_Leaders_Summits_of_Americas_.28ILSA.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Indigenous_Leaders_Summits_of_Americas_(ILSA)">Indigenous Leaders Summits of Americas (ILSA)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Indigenous Leaders Summits of Americas (ILSA)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5> 
      <p>With St Vincent and the Grenadines having at least two groups of indigenous persons<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> it is expected that there will be contributions from the SVG's on this topic at the next ILSAs.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The position of the OAS with respect to indigenous persons appears to be developing over the years. The following statements appear to capture the position of the OAS with respect to the ILSA: "The OAS has supported and participated in the organisation of Indigenous Leaders Summits of Americas (ILSA)" according to the OAS's website. The most recent "statement made by the Heads of State of the hemisphere was in the Declaration of Commitments of Port of Spain in 2009 – Paragraph 86 according to the OAS's website."<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Draft American Declaration of the Rights of the Indigenous Persons appear to be a working document. The last "Meeting for Negotiations in the Quest for Consensus on this area appeared to be Meeting Number (18) eighteen and is listed as being held in May 2015 according to the website."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_nations">European nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: European nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2013, Saint Vincent called for European nations to pay reparations for the <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slave trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Saint Vincent protests against <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>'s claim to give full effect to <a href="/wiki/Aves_(Bird)_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Aves (Bird) Island">Aves (Bird) Island</a>, which creates a Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/EEZ" class="mw-redirect" title="EEZ">EEZ</a>/<a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">continental shelf</a> extending over a large portion of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Economy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Economy of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png/220px-St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png/330px-St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png/440px-St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="855" data-file-height="668"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A proportional representation of St Vincent and the Grenadines' exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent,_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent,_Karibik_-_Kingstown_-_Looking_north_from_Fort_Charlotte_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Camden Park, St. Vincent
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Agriculture, dominated by <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">banana</a> production, is the most important sector of this lower-middle-income economy. The services sector, based mostly on a growing tourist industry, is also important. The government has been relatively unsuccessful at introducing new industries, and the <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Unemployment rate">unemployment rate</a> remains high at 19.8% in the 1991 census<sup id="cite_ref-popin_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popin-44">[44]</a></sup> to 15% in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-45">[45]</a></sup> The continuing dependence on a single crop represents the biggest obstacle to the islands' development as tropical storms wiped out substantial portions of bananas in many years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>There is a small manufacturing sector and a small offshore financial sector serving international businesses, and its secrecy laws have caused some international concern. There are increasing demands for international financial services like stock exchange and financial intermediaries financial activities in the country. In addition, the natives of <a href="/wiki/Bequia" title="Bequia">Bequia</a> are permitted to hunt up to four <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a> per year under <a href="/wiki/International_Whaling_Commission" title="International Whaling Commission">IWC</a> subsistence quotas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The tourism sector has considerable potential for development. The recent filming of the <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Pirates of the Caribbean films">Pirates of the Caribbean</a></i> movies on the island has helped to expose the country to more potential visitors and investors. Recent growth has been stimulated by strong activity in the construction sector and an improvement in tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-sids_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sids-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Argyle_International_Airport" title="Argyle International Airport">Argyle International Airport</a> is the country's new international airport.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The new facility opened on 14 February 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> replacing the existing <a href="/wiki/E.T._Joshua_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="E.T. Joshua Airport">E.T. Joshua Airport</a>. The airport is on the island's east coast about 8.3&nbsp;km (5.17 miles) from Kingstown.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Telecommunications in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Telecommunications in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2010, Saint Vincent and the Grenadines had 21,700 telephone land lines. Its land telephone system is fully automatic and covers the entire island and all of the inhabited Grenadine islands.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-45">[45]</a></sup> In 2002, there were 10,000 mobile phones.<sup id="cite_ref-about_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about-49">[49]</a></sup> By 2010, this number had increased to 131,800.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-45">[45]</a></sup> Mobile phone service is available in most areas of Saint Vincent as well as the Grenadines.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Saint Vincent has two ISPs (<a href="/wiki/Digicel" title="Digicel">Digicel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flow_(brand)" title="Flow (brand)">Flow</a>) that provide cellular telephone and internet service.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-50">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Demographics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Demographics of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The population as estimated in 2018 was 110,211.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-3">[3]</a></sup> The ethnic composition was 66% <a href="/wiki/African_descent" class="mw-redirect" title="African descent">African descent</a>, 19% of mixed descent, 6% East Indian, 4% <a href="/wiki/Europeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> (mainly Portuguese), 2% <a href="/wiki/Island_Carib" class="mw-redirect" title="Island Carib">Island Carib</a> and 3% others.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent_6-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook_–_St_Vincent-6">[6]</a></sup> Most Vincentians are the descendants of <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">African</a> people brought to the island to work on <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantations</a>. There are other ethnic groups such as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>) and <a href="/wiki/East_India" title="East India">East Indians</a>, both brought in to work on the plantations after the abolishing of slavery by the British living on the island. There is also a growing Chinese population.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vincentian_Creole" title="Vincentian Creole">Vincentian Creole</a>
      </div> 
      <p>English is the official language. Most Vincentians speak Vincentian Creole.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> English is used in education, government, religion, and other formal domains, while Creole (or 'dialect' as it is referred to locally) is used in informal situations such as in the home and among friends.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent,_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-St._Vincent%2C_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="2536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:St._Vincent,_Karibik_-_St._Mary%27s_R.C._School_%5E_St._Mary%27s_R.C._Cathedral_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Assumption_Cathedral,_Kingstown" title="Assumption Cathedral, Kingstown">Assumption Cathedral</a>, Kingstown
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2001 census, 81.5% of the population of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines identified themselves as <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>, 6.7% has another religion and 8.8% has no religion or did not state a religion (1.5%).<sup id="cite_ref-2001_census_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001_census-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a> constitutes the largest religious category, with 17.8% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Pentecostals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> are the second largest group (17.6%). The next largest group are <a href="/wiki/Methodists#Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodists">Methodists</a> (10.9% of the population), followed by <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a> (10.2%) and <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> (10.0%).
