Other Christians include <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.6%), <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> (7.5%), <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelicals</a> (2.8%), Church of God (2.5%), <a href="/wiki/Brethren_Christian" class="mw-redirect" title="Brethren Christian">Brethren Christian</a> (1.3%), and the <a href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvation Army">Salvation Army</a> (0.3%).<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 1991 and 2001 the number of Anglicans, Brethren, Methodists and Roman Catholics decreased, while the number of Pentecostals, Evangelicals and Seventh-day Adventists increased.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The number of non-Christians is small. These religious groups include the <a href="/wiki/Rastafari_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Rastafari movement">Rastafarians</a> (1.5% of the population), <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_West_Indies" title="Hinduism in the West Indies">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> (1.5%).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mustiquebeaches.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mustiquebeaches.jpg/220px-Mustiquebeaches.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mustiquebeaches.jpg/330px-Mustiquebeaches.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mustiquebeaches.jpg/440px-Mustiquebeaches.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="668"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mustiquebeaches.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The island of <a href="/wiki/Mustique" title="Mustique">Mustique</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Grenadines" title="Grenadines">Grenadines</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Cricket, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a> and association football are most popular among men whereas <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a> is most popular among women. Basketball, volleyball and tennis are also very popular.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's prime <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> league is the <a href="/wiki/NLA_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="NLA Premier League">NLA Premier League</a>, which provides its <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_national_football_team" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines national football team">national (association) football team</a> with most players. A notable Vincentian footballer is <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Hendrickson" title="Ezra Hendrickson">Ezra Hendrickson</a>, former national team captain who played at several Major League Soccer clubs in the United States and is now an assistant coach with the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Sounders_FC" title="Seattle Sounders FC">Seattle Sounders FC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sounders_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sounders-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country regularly participates at the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Basketball Championship">Caribbean Basketball Championship</a> where a <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines national basketball team">men's team</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_women%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines women's national basketball team">women's team</a> compete. Saint Vincent and the Grenadines also has its own <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines_national_rugby_union_team" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines national rugby union team">national rugby union team</a> which is ranked 84th in the world. Other notable sports played at the regional level include track and field.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Music of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Music of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Music popular in Saint Vincent and the Grenadines includes big drum, <a href="/wiki/Calypso_music" title="Calypso music">calypso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steelpan" title="Steelpan">steelpan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a>. String band music, quadrille and traditional storytelling are also popular. One of the most successful St Vincent natives is <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Lyttle" title="Kevin Lyttle">Kevin Lyttle</a>. He was named Cultural Ambassador for the Island 19 September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The national anthem of Saint Vincent and the Grenadines is "<a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent,_Land_so_beautiful" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent, Land so beautiful">Saint Vincent, Land so beautiful</a>", adopted upon independence in 1979.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Saint Vincent has twelve FM radio stations: 88.9 Adoration Fm,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> 89.1 Jem Radio, 89.7 NBC Radio, 95.7 and 105.7 <a href="/wiki/Praise_FM_(Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines)" title="Praise FM (Saint Vincent and the Grenadines)">Praise FM</a>, 96.7 Nice Radio, 97.1 Hot 97, 98.3 Star FM, 99.9 We FM, 103.7 Hitz, 102.7 EZee radio, 104.3 Xtreme FM and 106.9 Boom FM. There are several Internet radio stations including Chronicles Christian Radio.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> It has one television broadcast station ZBG-TV (SVGTV)<sup id="cite_ref-svgtv_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-svgtv-61">[61]</a></sup> and one cable television provider. </p>
      <p>St Vincent and the Grenadines Broadcasting Co-operation is the parent company for SVGTV, Magic 103.7.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

                   <li><a href="/wiki/Common_Fund_for_Commodities" title="Common Fund for Commodities">Common Fund for Commodities (CFC)</a></li> 
                   <li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Court_of_Justice" title="Caribbean Court of Justice">Court of Justice (CCJ)</a></li> 
                   <li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Disaster_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency">Disaster Emergency Management (CDEMA)</a></li>

                   <li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Institute_for_Meteorology_and_Hydrology" title="Caribbean Institute for Meteorology and Hydrology">Caribbean Institute for Meteorology and Hydrology</a></li> 
                   <li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Public_Health_Agency" title="Caribbean Public Health Agency">Public Health Agency (CARPHA)</a></li> 
                   <li><a href="/wiki/CARICOM_Single_Market_and_Economy" title="CARICOM Single Market and Economy">Single Market and Economy (CSME)</a></li>
                  </ul> 
                 </div></td>
